## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is an instantaneous population growth rate driven by current population size P (density dependence) and possibly explicit time t (seasonality, environmental change, interventions). With only (t, P) available, classical continuous-time population models are typically first-order ODEs of the form dP_dt = f(t, P).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Exponential growth with constant immigration: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 (open population with net influx)
- Linear per-capita trend in time: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (changing environment causing drifting growth rate)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (crowding/self-limitation as pairwise competition)
- General polynomial crowding: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (phenomenological density feedback)
- Logistic (Verhulst) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying capacity with linear density dependence)
- Theta-logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible density dependence curvature)
- Gompertz growth (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric slowing toward an upper bound)
- Richards-type generalized logistic (ODE form): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (adjustable sigmoidal shape)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative at low density and limited at high density)
- Weak Allee effect (saturating facilitation): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * P / (P + c3) (positive density dependence at low P plus carrying capacity)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - c4 * P) (periodic environment affecting growth rate)
- Harvesting/removal (constant effort): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (proportional mortality/harvest)
- Saturating harvest (Holling-II removal): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (P + c3) (removal limited by handling/time)
- Pulse disturbance / intervention: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * exp(-c3 * (t - c4)**2) (transient mortality or control centered at time c4)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth diagnosis: if dP_dt / P is ~constant, use c0 * P; if dP_dt / P decreases with P, include negative density dependence terms (e.g., -c * P**2 or logistic factors).
- Carrying capacity behavior: existence of a stable equilibrium P* > 0 suggests a factor that changes sign at P* (e.g., (1 - c * P) or (1 - (c * P)**theta)).
- Asymmetric approach to saturation: if growth slows early and approaches the ceiling gradually (more right-skewed than logistic), prefer Gompertz-like c0 * P * log(c1 / P).
- Allee signatures: if growth is negative at low P but positive at intermediate P, include an additional low-density zero (factor like (c * P - 1)) multiplying P.
- Seasonality: repeating oscillations in dP_dt at similar P levels imply explicit periodic forcing in t (sin/cos in the growth-rate prefactor).
- Long-term environmental trend: systematic drift in dP_dt over time at similar P suggests time-varying rate terms like (c0 + c1 * t) or (c0 + c1 * log(c2 * t + 1)).
- Harvest/removal identification: if dP_dt is reduced roughly proportionally across P, add -c * P; if reduction plateaus at high P, use saturating removal -c * P/(P + h).
- Pulse events: sharp transient drops or boosts at specific times are well captured by localized kernels in t such as exp(-c * (t - t0)**2) added to the baseline growth law.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$0.8678(-1 + P/6.058)(1 - P/14.185)P + 0.8678 P^{1/3} + 0.8678 P$$

Let me expand the first term:
$$(-1 + P/6.058)(1 - P/14.185) = -1 + P/14.185 + P/6.058 - P^2/(6.058 \times 14.185)$$
$$= -1 + P(1/14.185 + 1/6.058) - P^2/85.90$$

Multiplying by P:
$$= -P + P^2(1/14.185 + 1/6.058) - P^3/85.90$$

So the full GT is:
$$0.8678[-P + P^2(1/14.185 + 1/6.058) - P^3/85.90] + 0.8678 P^{1/3} + 0.8678 P$$

The $-P$ and $+P$ terms from the linear part cancel partially... let me compute:
- $0.8678 \times (-P) + 0.8678P = 0$ — they cancel!

So GT = $0.8678 P^{1/3} + 0.8678 P^2(1/14.185 + 1/6.058) - 0.8678 P^3/(6.058 \times 14.185)$

Computing constants:
- $1/14.185 + 1/6.058 \approx 0.07050 + 0.16507 = 0.23557$
- $0.8678 \times 0.23557 \approx 0.20442$ (coefficient of $P^2$)
- $6.058 \times 14.185 = 85.917$
- $0.8678/85.917 \approx 0.01010$ (coefficient of $P^3$, negative)

So GT ≈ $-0.01010 P^3 + 0.20442 P^2 + 0.8678 P^{1/3}$

### Candidate 24: $c0 P^3 + c1 P^2 + c2 P + P/(P+c3) + c4(P+c5)^{c6} + c7$

$c0 P^3 + c1 P^2 + c4 P^{1/3} + (1+c7)$ 

GT has no constant term. Set $c7 = -1$: $c0 P^3 + c1 P^2 + c4 P^{1/3}$ ✓
